Quranic Evidence for Two Capacities
Maturidi opens with Quranic evidence and first rational aspect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Quranic verses distinguish between capacity of means/causes and capacity of the act itself.

Core Idea
Quranic 'capacity' often refers to means, not the act.

In this passage, Imam Maturidi examines key Quranic verses to show that the word 'istiṭā‘a' (capacity) does not always refer to the power to perform an act. Sometimes it denotes the availability of means like health, wealth, or time. This distinction is crucial for understanding divine obligation and human responsibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening statement
Read the first sentence where Maturidi states the evidence for dividing capacity into two types. Note the two Quranic verses he cites: 58:4 and 9:42.
These verses are the foundation of the discussion.
2
Examine the first aspect
Focus on the argument about the kaffarah verse (58:4). Understand why the capacity mentioned there cannot be the capacity of the act itself because it refers to a two-month period.
3
Understand the hypocrites' example
Analyze how the hypocrites' excuse (9:42) is interpreted as lack of means (illness or wealth), not inability to perform the act of jihad.
God's explanation in 9:91-93 clarifies this.
4
Reflect on the distinction
Ask yourself: what difference does it make whether 'capacity' means means or act? Think about obligations like Hajj or fasting.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الدلالة على قسمة الاستطاعتين قول الله تعالى : لَمْ يَسْتَطِعْ فَإِطْعَامُ سِتِّينَ مِسْكِينًا ، وما قال : لَوْ اسْتَطَعْنَا لَخَرْجْنَا مَعَكُمْ . ثم الدلالة على أن الاستطاعة استطاعة الأسباب والأحوال لا استطاعة الفعل وجوه : أحدها أن قوله : فَمَنْ لَمْ يَسْتَطِعْ، وإنما هو صوم شهرين ، ولا أحد يعلم أن قدرة الفعل لا ترد تلك المدة ، ثبت أن المراد من ذلك استطاعة الوجود . ومثله أهل النفاق ، لم يكونوا يعلمون الاستطاعة التي لديها الأفعال ، وإنما أرادوا بذلك المرض أو فقد المال على ما بين الله تعالى بقوله : لَيْسَ عَلَى الضُّعَفَاءِ إلى قوله : إنَّمَا السَّبِيلُ عَلَى الَّذِينَ يَسْتَأْ ذِنُونَكَ وَهُمْ أَغْنِيَاءُ . ودليل آخر القول المعروف أن الاستطاعة المجود منها لا يبقى إلى مدة شهرين ، ولا استطاعة فعل الجهاد تبقى من وقت كونهم بالمدينة إلى أن يلقوا عدوا ، بل هي تتجدد وتحدث ، وقد لزمهم الخروج قبل العلم بأنها تحدث أولا وكذبوا بقولهم : لو استطعنا الخرجنا معكم ، وحققوا فى الأول نفى الاستطاعة ، فثبت أن المراد من ذلك استطاعة الأحوال والأسباب لا الأفعال ، ولا قوة إلا بالله وأيضا أنه لا يجوز أن يكون الله تعالى يعير قوما بالعناد فيما يعلم أنهم لا يعلمون ، وأن دليل العلم به لم يظهر لهم ، وقدرة الاحتمال التي يتكلم فيها بمع وقبل وتبقى ولا تبقى ، ليس لأحد من العوام تصور فى الأوهام ولا ترجع إليها عقولهم ، ثبت أن الرخصة والمعاينة فى أهل النفاق فما يدركون ويعرفون ، وأيد ذلك قوله : وَمَنْ لَمْ يَسْتَطِعْ مِنْكُمْ طَوْلاً ، وقوله : واللهِ عَلَى النَّاسِ حج البَيْتِ مَنِ اسْتَطَاعَ إِلَيْهِ
The evidence for the division of the two capacities is the saying of God Almighty: 'he cannot [fast] then feed sixty poor persons' (58:4), and what He said: 'If we had been able, we would have gone out with you' (9:42). Then the evidence that capacity (istiṭā‘a) is the capacity of causes and states, not the capacity of the act, [consists of] aspects: one of them is that His saying: 'Whoever does not have the capacity' (58:4) is only [about] fasting two months, and no one knows that the power of the act does not last that period; so it is established that what is meant by that is the capacity of existence. And similarly the hypocrites—they did not know the capacity by which actions occur, but they meant by that illness or lack of wealth, as God Almighty explained in His saying: 'There is no blame on the weak' (9:91) up to His saying: 'The way is only against those who ask permission of you while they are rich' (9:93). Another proof is the well-known saying that the capacity which is [referred to as] 'exerted' does not remain for a period of two months, and the capacity of the act of jihad does not remain from the time they were in Medina until they meet an enemy; rather it is renewed and occurs, and they were obliged to go out before knowing whether it occurs or not, and they lied by saying 'If we had been able, we would have gone out with you', and they affirmed initially the negation of capacity; so it is established that what is meant by that is the capacity of states and causes, not of acts. And there is no power except through God. And also: it is not permissible for God Almighty to reproach people for stubbornness in something He knows they do not know, and the evidence of knowledge of it has not appeared to them, and the power of possibility—which is spoken of with 'with' and 'before' and remains and does not remain—none of the common people have a concept of it in their imaginations nor do their intellects refer to it; so it is established that the concession and observation regarding the hypocrites [was about] what they perceive and know. And that is supported by His saying: 'And whoever among you does not have the capacity (ṭawl)' (4:25), and His saying: 'And due to God is the Hajj of the House for whoever has the capacity (istiṭā‘a) to it' (3:97).
Source pages p. 856

Commentary
This passage provides evidence for the division of capacity (istiṭā‘a) into two types: capacity of causes/states (asbāb wa aḥwāl) and capacity of the act itself. Maturidi begins by citing two Quranic verses: the kaffarah verse (58:4) which says 'he cannot [fast] then feed sixty poor persons'—here 'cannot' refers to inability to fast for two months, a capacity of health, not of the act itself. Similarly, the hypocrites' verse (9:42) where they say 'If we had been able, we would have gone out with you', but their lack was of means (health, wealth), not of the act of fighting. Then he gives rational proofs: (1) The capacity mentioned in the kaffarah verse concerns a period of two months, but the power of the act itself (qudrat al-fi‘l) does not last that long; therefore it must be capacity of existence (istiṭā‘at al-wujūd), i.e., health and means. (2) The hypocrites' capacity for jihad does not persist from Medina to the battlefield; it arises and dissolves with time and circumstances; they were obligated to go forth even without knowing if it would occur, so their claim 'if we were able' was a lie about their capacity of means. (3) God cannot rebuke people for something they are ignorant of and for which no evidence reached them; the abstract concept of a capacity that remains or does not remain is beyond common people's comprehension, so the reproach must refer to observable capacities like wealth and health. He supports this with the verse about marriage capacity (4:25) and the Hajj verse (3:97) where 'capacity' clearly means financial and physical ability, not a power that endures until the act.

Key Terms
استطاعة
استطاعة الأسباب
استطاعة الفعل
قدرة الفعل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That every occurrence of 'cannot' in the Quran refers to inability to perform the act itself.
Correction: Maturidi shows that in verses about kaffarah and jihad, 'cannot' refers to lack of means (health, wealth), not the act's capacity.

Checkpoint
Why does Maturidi argue that the 'capacity' mentioned in the kaffarah verse (58:4) is not the capacity of the act?
A) Because the verse mentions feeding, not fasting
B) Because the capacity of the act does not last two months
C) Because the hypocrites were not obligated to fast
D) Because God does not burden a soul beyond its capacity

Key Takeaway
The Quran uses 'istiṭā‘a' sometimes for capacity of means, not the act itself.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'I can't' to a religious obligation or good deed, do you honestly examine whether it is a lack of means (time, health, wealth) or a lack of will? Which of the two capacities is truly absent?
?
The hypocrites in the verse excused themselves with lack of means while God knew their hearts. Are you using lack of means as a cover for not wanting to sacrifice? What would it take for you to test your own sincerity and act even when means are scarce?
?
If God holds you accountable for the capacity of means, what are you doing to strengthen your means (health, wealth, time) so that they become enablers, not excuses, for obedience? Write one practical step you will take this week.

Rational Arguments for Capacity of Causes
Maturidi presents two more rational proofs and supporting verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proofs that capacity (istiṭā‘a) is for causes and states, not for the act itself.

Core Idea
Capacity of the act is momentary; only means persist.

Maturidi continues with additional rational arguments to solidify the distinction. He argues that the capacity for jihad cannot remain from Medina to the battlefield, and that God cannot reproach people for what they cannot know. These points further demonstrate that when the Quran mentions 'capacity', it refers to observable circumstances like health and wealth.

Guided Path
1
Read the second proof
Read the argument that the 'capacity' of jihad does not persist from Medina to the battlefield; it renews with time and place. The hypocrites' lie was about means, not act-power.
2
Analyze the third proof
Understand why God cannot rebuke people for something they are ignorant of and for which no evidence came. The abstract notion of a capacity that remains or not is beyond common understanding.
3
Connect supporting verses
Look at the two supporting verses (4:25 and 3:97) where 'capacity' clearly means financial or physical ability.
4
Synthesize the overall argument
Ask yourself: how do these rational proofs together show that most Quranic uses of 'istiṭā‘a' refer to means?

According to the third proof, why can't God reproach the hypocrites for lacking an abstract capacity?
A) Because they were rich

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'I can't' regarding an Islamic obligation, are you sure it is a lack of capacity of the act, or are you excusing yourself from using the means (health, wealth, time) that Allah has given you? What would it take for you to honestly answer this question?
?
The hypocrites pretended they lacked the means, but they actually had them. In what areas of your life do you claim inability while having the resources? How can you stop lying to yourself and to Allah?
?
Maturidi teaches that God does not reproach people for what they do not know if evidence has not reached them. Are you seeking out the evidence for what Allah asks of you, or are you content with ignorance and then blaming Allah for your lack of action? What step will you take today to seek that evidence?

Evidence for the Division of Two Capacities from the Quran
Maturidi cites two Quranic verses as evidence for the division of istita'a.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Quran itself distinguishes between two types of capacity (istita'a): capacity of means and capacity of the act, as shown in two key verses.

Core Idea
The Quran hints at two capacities: one for expiation, one for jihad.

Maturidi begins his argument by citing two Quranic verses that implicitly reveal a division in the concept of istita'a. These verses are used as foundational evidence that capacity can refer either to means or to the act itself. This lesson examines these verses and their relevance.

Guided Path
1
Read the two verses
Read the Arabic of both verses carefully. Note how the word 'istita'a' appears in different contexts.
One is about expiation, the other about jihad excuse.
2
Understand the division
Maturidi claims these verses show a division. Ask: how does each verse point to a different kind of capacity?
3
Connect to the broader argument
This division is the stepping stone for the proofs that follow. Grasp it now to appreciate the next lesson.
The next lesson details the proofs.

الدلالة على قسمة الاستطاعتين قول الله تعالى: {لَمْ يَسْتَطِعْ فَإِطْعَامُ سِتِّينَ مِسْكِينًا}[المجادلة:٤]، وما قال: {لَوِ اسْتَطَعْنَا لَخَرَجْنَا مَعَكُمْ}[التوبة:٤٢]. ثم الدلالة على أن الاستطاعة استطاعة الأسباب والأحوال لا استطاعة الفعل وجوه: أحدها أن قوله: {فَمَنْ لَمْ يَسْتَطِعْ} إنما هو صوم شهرين، ولا أحد يعلم أن قدرة الفعل لا تنقضي تلك المدة، فثبت أن المراد من ذلك استطاعة الوجود. ومثله أهل النفاق، لم يكونوا يعلمون الاستطاعة التي لديها الأفعال، وإنما أرادوا بذلك المرض أو فقد المال على ما بين الله تعالى بقوله: {لَيْسَ عَلَى الضُّعَفَاءِ} إلى قوله: {إِنَّمَا السَّبِيلُ عَلَى الَّذِينَ يَسْتَأْذِنُونَكَ وَهُمْ أَغْنِيَاءُ}[التوبة:٩١-٩٣]. ودليل آخر: القول المعروف أن الاستطاعة المجود منها لا يبقى إلى مدة شهرين، ولا استطاعة فعل الجهاد تبقى من وقت كونهم بالمدينة إلى أن يلقوا عدوا، بل هي تتجدد وتحدث، وقد لزمهم الخروج قبل العلم بأنها تحدث أولا وكذبوا بقولهم: لو استطعنا لخرجنا معكم، وحققوا في الأول نفي الاستطاعة، فثبت أن المراد من ذلك استطاعة الأحوال والأسباب لا الأفعال، ولا قوة إلا بالله. وأيضا أنه لا يجوز أن يكون الله تعالى يعير قوما بالعناد فيما يعلم أنهم لا يعلمون، وأن دليل العلم به لم يظهر لهم، وقدرة الاحتمال التي يتكلم فيها بمع وقبل وتبقى ولا تبقى، ليس لأحد من العوام تصور في الأوهام ولا ترجع إليها عقولهم، ثبت أن الرخصة والمعاينة في أهل النفاق فما يدركون ويعرفون، وأيد ذلك قوله: {وَمَنْ لَمْ يَسْتَطِعْ مِنْكُمْ طَوْلاً}[النساء:٢٥]، وقوله: {وَلِلَّهِ عَلَى النَّاسِ حِجُّ الْبَيْتِ مَنِ اسْتَطَاعَ إِلَيْهِ سَبِيلاً}[آل عمران:٩٧].
The evidence for the division of the two capacities is the saying of Allah Almighty: 'He who cannot find [means] – then a fast of sixty days' [58:4], and His saying: 'If we had been able, we would have gone out with you' [9:42]. Then the evidence that capacity is capacity of causes and states, not capacity of the act, has several aspects: One of them is that His saying: 'Then whoever cannot find [means]' (58:4) refers to a fast of two months, and no one knows that the power of the act does not expire in that period; thus it is established that what is meant by that is the capacity of existence. Similarly, the people of hypocrisy (munafiqun) did not know the capacity that accompanies actions; rather they intended by that illness or lack of wealth, as Allah Almighty has explained with His saying: 'There is no blame on the weak' up to His saying: 'The blame is only upon those who ask permission of you while they are rich' [9:91-93]. Another proof: the well-known statement that the capacity that is found does not remain for a period of two months, and the capacity for the act of jihad does not remain from the time of their being in Medina until they meet an enemy; rather it is renewed and occurs. And they were obliged to go out before knowing whether it occurs first, and they were belied by their saying: 'If we had been able, we would have gone out with you.' And they established in the first [instance] the negation of capacity, so it is established that what is meant by that is the capacity of states and causes, not of actions. And there is no power except with Allah. And also, it is not permissible for Allah Almighty to reproach a people for obstinacy regarding what He knows they do not know, and the proof of knowledge of it has not appeared to them. And the capacity of [؟] which is spoken of with 'with' and 'before', and remains and does not remain, there is for none of the common people a conceptualization in fantasies, nor do their intellects refer to them. It is established that permission and observation in the people of hypocrisy are only what they perceive and know. And that is supported by His saying: 'And whoever among you cannot find [means] for [marriage]' [4:25], and His saying: 'And for Allah is the duty of pilgrimage to the House for whoever is able to find a way to it' [3:97].
Source pages p. 856

Commentary
This passage is a proof-based argument defining the two types of capacity (istita'a) and demonstrating that the Quranic usage often refers to capacity of means (istita'at al-asbab wa al-ahwal) rather than capacity of the act itself. Maturidi begins by citing two Quranic verses: (58:4) about expiation for zihar requiring fasting if one cannot free a slave, and (9:42) where the hypocrites use 'if we had been able' as an excuse not to join jihad. He then presents multiple aspects of evidence. The first evidence is that the verse 'So whoever cannot find [means]' (58:4) speaks of fasting two months as an alternative, and no one understands the capacity to perform the act to last that long; thus it must refer to capacity of existence (i.e., ability in terms of means). Second, the hypocrites in (9:42) did not claim inability to perform the act of jihad itself but rather illness or lack of resources, as clarified in (9:91-93). The second proof: the well-known principle that the capacity that is found does not persist for two months; likewise, the capacity for jihad does not remain from their being in Medina until battle, but is renewed. The hypocrites were blamed for saying 'if we had been able' while they were actually able in terms of means, proving that the intended capacity is that of states and causes, not actions. The third proof: it is impossible for Allah to blame people for obstinacy regarding something they do not know and for which no evidence has reached them. The common people cannot conceptualize the kind of capacity that is spoken of in terms of before and after, remaining or not remaining. Thus, the blame and reproach in the hypocrites' case is only for what they perceive and know. Maturidi supports this by citing verses about marriage capacity (4:25) and pilgrimage (3:97), which clearly refer to ability of means.

Key Terms
استطاعة (istita'a)
الاستطاعتين (two capacities)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think istita'a only refers to one's ability to perform an action directly.
Correction: Maturidi shows that the Quran uses istita'a to mean capacity of means, as in these verses.

Checkpoint
Which verse is used to show that capacity can mean having the means to free a slave?
A) 58:4
B) 9:42
C) 4:25
D) 3:97

Key Takeaway
The Quran provides evidence that istita'a can refer to capacity of means, not just capacity of the act.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'I can't' to a religious obligation, which capacity are you truly lacking—means or will? How does this lesson expose your excuses?
?
The hypocrites in 9:42 claimed inability but had means. When have you used a lack of resources to justify a lack of action? What would it take for you to honestly assess your capacity before Allah?
?
If you possess the means (time, wealth, health) to perform a good deed but fail to act, does your claim of inability reveal a deeper spiritual weakness? What will you change after learning this distinction?

Proofs that Istita'a Refers to Capacity of Means
Maturidi presents three proofs that istita'a is capacity of means.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's three proofs that the capacity mentioned in the Quran is capacity of means (causes and states) rather than capacity of the act.

Core Idea
Capacity of means can expire and is what people know.

Having established the division, Maturidi now offers detailed proofs to show that when the Quran speaks of istita'a, it typically means capacity of means (istita'at al-asbab wa al-ahwal) and not the capacity to perform the act itself. He provides multiple arguments from the verses themselves and from logical reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the first proof about fasting
The verse about zihar (58:4) mentions fasting for two months. Maturidi argues that capacity of the act does not last that long; thus the verse refers to capacity of means.
2
Read the second proof about jihad
The hypocrites' excuse in 9:42 is clarified by verses 9:91-93: they lacked means (illness/wealth). Also, capacity for jihad is renewed, not permanent.
3
Read the third proof about reproach
Allah cannot reproach people for obstinacy over something unknown. The common people cannot conceptualize capacity that remains or not. So the reproach is about what they know: means.
4
Supporting verses
Maturidi cites 4:25 and 3:97 which clearly refer to capacity of means.
These reinforce the conclusion.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi's third proof, why is it not permissible for Allah to reproach people for obstinacy regarding something they do not know?
A) Because people are blameless for ignorance
B) Because the proof of knowledge has not appeared to them

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you find yourself saying 'I can't' about a religious obligation (like Hajj, fasting, or giving charity), are you honest about whether it's truly a lack of means or a lack of will? Which excuses have you used that sound like the hypocrites' claim of inability while you actually had the means?
?
Maturidi argues that Allah does not reproach people for what they cannot know or conceptualize. Is there a religious duty you avoid because you think you cannot understand it, even though the knowledge is accessible? How does this lesson call you to take responsibility for seeking the means to understand and act?
?
The hypocrites blamed their lack of action on 'inability' when they had the means. Think of a time you blamed circumstances for not fulfilling a commitment to Allah. If you were to strip away all excuses and ask yourself if you truly lacked the means (time, health, wealth) or simply the will, what would you find?

Definition of the Second Type of Capacity
Maturidi defines the second type of capacity and interprets two Quranic verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's definition of the second type of capacity (istita'a) as the capacity of means and states, and how he interprets Quranic verses about burdening within capacity (2:286, 2:233) to refer to causes and states, not the act itself.

Core Idea
The second type of capacity is a condition for being addressed by divine discourse.

Imam Maturidi begins this section by clarifying a key distinction in the concept of human capacity. He explains that there is a type of capacity that is a necessary condition for being addressed by divine commands, and he roots this in Quranic verses. This lesson unpacks his definition and his interpretation of two famous verses.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition and consensus
Read the opening sentence carefully. Maturidi states that this type of capacity is agreed upon as necessary for divine discourse to be binding. Note the phrase 'la yalzamu dunahu'.
This is the second type of capacity, not the capacity of the act itself.
2
Examine the Quranic verses
Maturidi cites two verses: 'Allah does not burden any soul except its capacity' (2:286) and 'no soul is burdened except its capacity' (2:233). He says they are mentioned with regard to causes and states, not the occurrence of actions.
Understand that 'wus'ah' here refers to capacity of means.
3
Reflect on the implication
Consider why Maturidi makes this distinction. This helps separate the capacity that is a prerequisite for being addressed from the capacity to perform the act itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا النوع مما أجمع على أن الخطاب لا يلزم دونه، وأنه الاستطاعات التي لا يغير من عدمها بترك الفعل ولا يخاطب به دون استكمال. وعلى ذلك تأويل قوله: {لا يُكَلِّفُ اللَّهُ نَفْسًا إِلا وُسْعَهَا}[البقرة:٢٨٦]، وقوله: {وَعَلَى الْمَوْلُودِ لَهُ رِزْقُهُنَّ وَكِسْوَتُهُنَّ بِالْمَعْرُوفِ لا تُكَلِّفُ نَفْسٌ إِلا وُسْعَهَا}[البقرة:٢٣٣]، إنها مذكورة عند ذكر الأسباب والأحوال دون وقوع الأفعال. وعلى ذلك قول من يحقق للعباد الفعل وهو النظر من وجهين: أحدهما إحالة الأمر باستعمال سبب ليس [له]، وهذه أسباب: فيقال: أبصر ولا بصر، أو مد يدك ولا يد، والثاني أن الأمر والنهي إنما هما في أسداء الشكر وتحذير الكفران، فلا يحتمل أن يفعل فيما لم يظهر ثمة نعمة ولا احتمل معرفتها الوسع، ولا قوة إلا بالله. والدلالة على الاستطاعة الأخرى قوله تعالى: {مَا كَانُوا يَسْتَطِيعُونَ السَّمْعَ}[هود:٢٠]، وقول صاحب موسى: {إِنَّكَ لَنْ تَسْتَطِيعَ مَعِيَ صَبْرًا}[الكهف:٦٧]، ثم قال: {أَلَمْ أَقُلْ لَكَ إِنَّكَ لَنْ تَسْتَطِيعَ مَعِيَ صَبْرًا}[الكهف:٧٥]، ثم قال: {ذَلِكَ تَأْوِيلُ مَا لَمْ تَسْتَطِعْ عَلَيْهِ صَبْرًا}[الكهف:٨٢]، على تحقيق قدرة الأحوال: نفاها إذ زالت الأفعال، وكذلك قوله: {فَاتَّقُوا اللَّهَ مَا اسْتَطَعْتُمْ}[التغابن:١٦]، وغير ذلك. ثم الدليل على لزوم الكلفة دون حقيقة هذا النوع من القدرة السمع والعقل. فأما السمع فما أخبرت من الآيات على نفي الاستطاعة، ثم الأمر والنهي والتعيير.
This type is that which is agreed upon that discourse (khitab) is not binding without it, and that these are capacities the absence of which does not change by abandoning the act, nor is [one] addressed without their completion. And upon that is the interpretation of His saying: 'Allah does not burden any soul except its capacity' [2:286], and His saying: 'And upon the father is their provision and clothing according to what is acceptable, no soul is burdened except its capacity' [2:233]; they are mentioned with regard to causes and states, not the occurrence of actions. And upon that is the saying of one who confirms the act for servants, and it is an examination from two aspects: One of them is the impossibility of commanding the use of a cause that [one does] not [have] – and these are causes: so it is said: 'See while not seeing,' or 'Stretch your hand while not having a hand.' The second is that command and prohibition are only regarding giving thanks and warning against ingratitude; so it is not possible that it be done regarding something where no blessing has appeared nor the capacity to know it [exists]. And there is no power except with Allah. And the evidence for the other capacity is the saying of Allah Almighty: 'They were not able to hear' [11:20], and the saying of the companion of Moses: 'Indeed you will not be able to have patience with me' [18:67], then he said: 'Did I not say to you that you will not be able to have patience with me?' [18:75], then he said: 'That is the interpretation of that for which you were not able to have patience' [18:82], upon the confirmation of the capacity of states: he negated it when actions ceased. And likewise His saying: 'So fear Allah as much as you are able' [64:16], and other [verses]. Then the evidence for the obligation of responsibility (kulfa) without the reality of this type of capacity is [from] hearing (sam') and reason (aql). As for hearing, it is what the verses inform of the negation of capacity, then command, prohibition, and reproach.
Source pages p. 857

Commentary
This passage discusses the second type of capacity (istita'a) and its role in obligation. Maturidi states that this type (capacity of means/states) is agreed upon as necessary for a person to be addressed by divine commands. These capacities are such that their absence does not change by abandoning the act, and one is not addressed without their completion. He then interprets two Quranic verses (2:286 and 2:233) about burdening within capacity, showing they refer to causes and states, not the acts themselves. Next, he presents an argument from two aspects regarding 'one who confirms the act for servants' (i.e., those who affirm human agency). First, it is impossible to command using a cause one does not possess, e.g., commanding sight without eyes or extending a hand without a hand. Second, command and prohibition only pertain to giving thanks or avoiding ingratitude, which presupposes a blessing to be grateful for; one cannot be obligated regarding something where no blessing or capacity to know it has appeared. Then he provides evidence for the other capacity (other than act) from various verses: 'They were not able to hear' (11:20) refers to inability due to circumstances; the story of Moses and Khidr uses 'you will not be able to have patience' which is a capacity of state, negated when actions ceased; and 'Fear Allah as much as you are able' (64:16) also indicates capacity of means. Finally, he introduces the evidence for the obligation of responsibility (kulfa) without the reality of this type of capacity from two sources: sam' (revelation) and aql (reason). The sam' includes the verses that negate capacity while still imposing commands, prohibition, and reproach. The argument appears to be that obligation can be based on revealed texts and rational considerations even if one does not possess the full capacity of the act itself. The text ends with 'فأما السمع' suggesting more detail follows beyond the window.

Key Terms
الخطاب (khitab)
الكلفة (kulfa)
الاستطاعات (istita'at)
الوسع (wus')

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, the Quranic verses 'Allah does not burden any soul except its capacity' refer to what?
A) The capacity to perform the act itself
B) Causes and states, not the occurrence of actions
C) The impossibility of obligation
D) The capacity of hearing and sight

Key Takeaway
The second type of capacity is a prerequisite for divine address, and Quranic verses on 'burdening within capacity' refer to causes and states, not acts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you feel a command of Allah is too heavy, do you pause to consider that He has already provided you with the necessary means and states to fulfill it? How does this understanding change your response to difficult obligations?
?
Maturidi teaches that the second type of capacity is a condition for being addressed. Are you truly using the capacities Allah has given you—health, time, resources—to respond to His commands? In what one area are you negligent, and what will you do about it today?
?
Have you ever excused yourself from an Islamic obligation by claiming you lacked the capacity, only to realize later that the lack was not in the means but in your resolve? What does this lesson teach you about sincerity when seeking excuses before Allah?

Two-Aspect Argument and Evidence for Capacity of States
Maturidi presents a two-aspect argument and Quranic evidence for capacity of states.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two-aspect argument that confirms human agency and the Quranic evidence for the capacity of states.

Core Idea
Commanding without means is impossible; obligation rests on blessings received.

Maturidi now elaborates on the nature of human capacity by presenting a two-part argument that confirms human agency. He then draws on Quranic verses to demonstrate the capacity of states—a capacity that fluctuates with circumstances. This lesson traces his reasoning and the scriptural proofs.

Guided Path
1
Understand the first aspect
The first aspect: it is impossible to command someone to use a cause they do not possess. Examples: 'see while not seeing' or 'stretch your hand while not having a hand.'
This highlights that commands must be possible with the available means.
2
Understand the second aspect
The second aspect: command and prohibition are only about giving thanks and warning against ingratitude. Therefore, obligation requires a prior blessing and the capacity to know it.
This ties obligation to prior divine favor.
3
Review Quranic evidence for capacity of states
Maturidi cites several verses: 'They were not able to hear' (11:20); the Moses-Khidr story (18:67,75,82); 'Fear Allah as much as you are able' (64:16). He interprets these as confirming capacity of states, negated when actions cease.
These verses show capacity varies with states, not acts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا النوع مما أجمع على أن الخطاب لا يلزم دونه، وأنه الاستطاعات التي لا يغير من عدمها بترك الفعل ولا يخاطب به دون استكمال. وعلى ذلك تأويل قوله: {لا يُكَلِّفُ اللَّهُ نَفْسًا إِلا وُسْعَهَا}[البقرة:٢٨٦]، وقوله: {وَعَلَى الْمَوْلُودِ لَهُ رِزْقُهُنَّ وَكِسْوَتُهُنَّ بِالْمَعْرُوفِ لا تُكَلِّفُ نَفْسٌ إِلا وُسْعَهَا}[البقرة:٢٣٣]، إنها مذكورة عند ذكر الأسباب والأحوال دون وقوع الأفعال. وعلى ذلك قول من يحقق للعباد الفعل وهو النظر من وجهين: أحدهما إحالة الأمر باستعمال سبب ليس [له]، وهذه أسباب: فيقال: أبصر ولا بصر، أو مد يدك ولا يد، والثاني أن الأمر والنهي إنما هما في أسداء الشكر وتحذير الكفران، فلا يحتمل أن يفعل فيما لم يظهر ثمة نعمة ولا احتمل معرفتها الوسع، ولا قوة إلا بالله. والدلالة على الاستطاعة الأخرى قوله تعالى: {مَا كَانُوا يَسْتَطِيعُونَ السَّمْعَ}[هود:٢٠]، وقول صاحب موسى: {إِنَّكَ لَنْ تَسْتَطِيعَ مَعِيَ صَبْرًا}[الكهف:٦٧]، ثم قال: {أَلَمْ أَقُلْ لَكَ إِنَّكَ لَنْ تَسْتَطِيعَ مَعِيَ صَبْرًا}[الكهف:٧٥]، ثم قال: {ذَلِكَ تَأْوِيلُ مَا لَمْ تَسْتَطِعْ عَلَيْهِ صَبْرًا}[الكهف:٨٢]، على تحقيق قدرة الأحوال: نفاها إذ زالت الأفعال، وكذلك قوله: {فَاتَّقُوا اللَّهَ مَا اسْتَطَعْتُمْ}[التغابن:١٦]، وغير ذلك. ثم الدليل على لزوم الكلفة دون حقيقة هذا النوع من القدرة السمع والعقل. فأما السمع فما أخبرت من الآيات على نفي الاستطاعة، ثم الأمر والنهي والتعيير.
This type is that which is agreed upon that discourse (khitab) is not binding without it, and that these are capacities the absence of which does not change by abandoning the act, nor is [one] addressed without their completion. And upon that is the interpretation of His saying: 'Allah does not burden any soul except its capacity' [2:286], and His saying: 'And upon the father is their provision and clothing according to what is acceptable, no soul is burdened except its capacity' [2:233]; they are mentioned with regard to causes and states, not the occurrence of actions. And upon that is the saying of one who confirms the act for servants, and it is an examination from two aspects: One of them is the impossibility of commanding the use of a cause that [one does] not [have] – and these are causes: so it is said: 'See while not seeing,' or 'Stretch your hand while not having a hand.' The second is that command and prohibition are only regarding giving thanks and warning against ingratitude; so it is not possible that it be done regarding something where no blessing has appeared nor the capacity to know it [exists]. And there is no power except with Allah. And the evidence for the other capacity is the saying of Allah Almighty: 'They were not able to hear' [11:20], and the saying of the companion of Moses: 'Indeed you will not be able to have patience with me' [18:67], then he said: 'Did I not say to you that you will not be able to have patience with me?' [18:75], then he said: 'That is the interpretation of that for which you were not able to have patience' [18:82], upon the confirmation of the capacity of states: he negated it when actions ceased. And likewise His saying: 'So fear Allah as much as you are able' [64:16], and other [verses]. Then the evidence for the obligation of responsibility (kulfa) without the reality of this type of capacity is [from] hearing (sam') and reason (aql). As for hearing, it is what the verses inform of the negation of capacity, then command, prohibition, and reproach.
Source pages p. 857

Commentary
This passage discusses the second type of capacity (istita'a) and its role in obligation. Maturidi states that this type (capacity of means/states) is agreed upon as necessary for a person to be addressed by divine commands. These capacities are such that their absence does not change by abandoning the act, and one is not addressed without their completion. He then interprets two Quranic verses (2:286 and 2:233) about burdening within capacity, showing they refer to causes and states, not the acts themselves. Next, he presents an argument from two aspects regarding 'one who confirms the act for servants' (i.e., those who affirm human agency). First, it is impossible to command using a cause one does not possess, e.g., commanding sight without eyes or extending a hand without a hand. Second, command and prohibition only pertain to giving thanks or avoiding ingratitude, which presupposes a blessing to be grateful for; one cannot be obligated regarding something where no blessing or capacity to know it has appeared. Then he provides evidence for the other capacity (other than act) from various verses: 'They were not able to hear' (11:20) refers to inability due to circumstances; the story of Moses and Khidr uses 'you will not be able to have patience' which is a capacity of state, negated when actions ceased; and 'Fear Allah as much as you are able' (64:16) also indicates capacity of means. Finally, he introduces the evidence for the obligation of responsibility (kulfa) without the reality of this type of capacity from two sources: sam' (revelation) and aql (reason). The sam' includes the verses that negate capacity while still imposing commands, prohibition, and reproach. The argument appears to be that obligation can be based on revealed texts and rational considerations even if one does not possess the full capacity of the act itself. The text ends with 'فأما السمع' suggesting more detail follows beyond the window.

Key Terms
قدرة الأحوال (qudrat al-ahwal)
إسداء الشكر (isda' al-shukr)
الكفران (kufran)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All Quranic references to 'inability' refer to lack of power to act
Correction: Maturidi distinguishes capacity of state/means from capacity of act; these verses refer to the former.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi's two-aspect argument, what makes it impossible to command a person to use a cause they do not have?
A) The blessing has not appeared
B) The act is not their own
C) They lack the means
D) They are not responsible

Key Takeaway
The two-aspect argument confirms that obligation requires means and blessings, and Quranic verses demonstrate the capacity of states.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever made an excuse for disobeying Allah by claiming you lacked the means, when in fact you had the ability in your state? What does this lesson teach you about the blessings you already possess?
?
When you reflect on the blessings Allah has given you – sight, hearing, patience – are you using them to give thanks or to ingratitude? Which of these blessings have you taken for granted today?
?
The lesson says obligation rests on blessings received. If you were to truly account for every blessing you have, what command of Allah are you neglecting that you actually have no excuse to ignore? What will you do about it starting now?

Obligation and Its Basis in Revelation and Reason
Maturidi argues that obligation (kulfa) does not require full capacity, citing revelation and reason.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's claim that the obligation of responsibility does not require the reality of the capacity of the act itself, and that it is established by both revelation and reason.

Core Idea
Obligation is valid even without full capacity, as proven by revelation and reason.

In the final part of the passage, Maturidi turns to a crucial point: being responsible (kulfa) does not depend on having the actual capacity to perform the act. Instead, the evidence for obligation comes from two sources: revelation (sam') and reason (aql). This lesson explores the beginning of his argument, focusing on the revealed evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the claim
Maturidi states: 'The evidence for the obligation of responsibility without the reality of this type of capacity is from hearing (sam') and reason (aql).'
This is a clear thesis.
2
Understand the revealed evidence
The revealed evidence consists of verses that negate capacity yet still impose command, prohibition, and reproach. Examples are the verses cited earlier.
The text breaks off, but the point is that even where capacity is negated, obligation remains.
3
Note the role of reason
Although the passage ends with 'As for hearing...', reason (aql) is mentioned as a second source. We infer that rational arguments also support obligation without capacity.

Refutation of the Claim That Humans Can Thwart God's Will
Al-Maturidi refutes those who claim humans have power to oppose God's decrees.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why claiming that humans can thwart God's will leads to absurd and blasphemous conclusions.

Core Idea
Human power cannot oppose God's will; to claim otherwise is to degrade God.

This passage from Imam al-Maturidi's Kitab al-Tawhid confronts a dangerous assumption: that human free will could override God's decree. Al-Maturidi argues that such a claim logically forces one to attribute imperfections to God—such as foolishness, ignorance, and breaking promises—which are impossible for the Divine. He then warns that this reasoning ultimately diminishes God's sovereignty, making Him dependent on His creation. Let's examine his argument closely.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once and then its English translation. Notice the tone: al-Maturidi is refuting a specific group that claims humans can oppose God.
The language is dense and theological. Read slowly.
2
Identify the absurd consequences
Al-Maturidi lists several impossible attributes that would be attributed to God if humans could thwart His will. Find them: making God foolish, ignorant, breaking promises.
These are all impossible for God.
3
Understand the theological principle
The key principle is that God cannot be subject to human power. Al-Maturidi finds it astonishing that anyone would think God could empower someone to nullify His lordship.
This ties to divine transcendence.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Al-Maturidi concludes that this view would make God subordinate to humans, which is a monstrous saying. Reflect on why this is incompatible with tawhid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أخبر به ، وعلى أن يتلف ما أراد الله إبقاءه قدر على تسفيه الله وتجهيله وخلفه في الوعد ، ومن ذلك وصفه ليس بإله ، وبمثله نفوا قول الثنوية . مع ما في هذا أمر عجيب أن يكون الله يقوى أحدا على نقض ربوبيته ؛ إذ ملك تصييره كاذبا وقدر على جمله جاهلا ، وعن وفاء ما وعده عاجزا . وهذا النوع من الأقدار لا يفعله أسفه السفهاء، فكيف أحكم الحاكمين ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . وعلى قول هؤلاء يكون للبشر قدرة نقض تدبير العالم ، وللرسل قوة أن لا يظهروا الله حجة في الأرض ، وأن يمتنع كل منهم عن الوجه الذي عليه مضى تدبير ، وهو مبنى على كون أحواله على أيدى البشر وخلق الأرض والسماء ، والله تعالى لم يكن له قدرة على خلق تلك الأفعال والأحوال على أيديهم ، ولهم قدرة على أن لا يفعلوا شيئا من ذلك ، فإذا لهم عليه أرفع المن وأعلى النعم ؛ إذ على القدرة في منع تقديره ونفاذ تدبيره فعلوا الذى به قام تدبيره وتم ملكه وسلطانه وعلى ما دبر وشاء ، وذلك أوحش قول وبالله التوفيق .
He informed that, and that if he intends to destroy what God wanted to preserve, he is capable of making God foolish, ignorant, and a breaker of promise, and from that is describing Him as not a god, and by similar they refuted the saying of the Dualists. Along with this is an amazing matter: that God should empower someone to nullify His lordship, since he possesses making Him a liar and is able to make Him ignorant, and unable to fulfill what He promised. And this type of decrees is not done by the most foolish of fools, so how by the most wise of rulers, and there is no power except with God. And according to the saying of these, humans have the power to nullify the management of the world, and the messengers have the power not to manifest God's proof on earth, and that each of them can refrain from the way upon which management proceeded, and it is based on that His states are at the hands of humans and the creation of earth and heaven, and God Almighty had no power to create those actions and states upon their hands, and they have the power not to do any of that, so they have upon Him the highest favor and greatest grace; since upon the power to prevent His decree and the penetration of His management, they did that by which His management stood and His kingdom and authority were completed and upon what He planned and willed, and that is the most dreadful saying, and with God is success.
Source pages p. 859

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of those who claim that humans can oppose or thwart God's will. The author argues that if humans had the power to destroy what God wants to preserve, they would be able to make God foolish, ignorant, and a breaker of promises—attributes that are impossible for God. Such a claim would also entail describing God as not truly divine, which is refuted by the example of the Dualists. The author finds it astonishing that God would empower anyone to nullify His lordship, making Him a liar, ignorant, and unable to fulfill His promises. This type of decree is not done even by the most foolish, so how could the Most Wise do it? The author then points out that on this erroneous view, humans would have the power to nullify the management of the world, and messengers could prevent God's proof from being manifested. This would imply that God had no power to create actions through them, while they had the power not to do anything, thus they would have the highest favor over God—a monstrous statement. The passage concludes with seeking God's success.

Key Terms
قدرة
تدبير
تسفيه
خلف الوعد
الثنوية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Humans have independent power to oppose or thwart God's will.
Correction: Al-Maturidi shows that such a claim leads to attributing impossibility to God (foolishness, ignorance, breaking promises) and undermines His sovereignty. Therefore, human free will is subordinate to God's will.

Checkpoint
What does Al-Maturidi argue would be the consequence of claiming that humans can thwart God's will?
A) Humans would be more powerful than angels
B) God would be described as foolish, ignorant, and a breaker of promises
C) Humans would become prophets
D) God's mercy would be unlimited

Key Takeaway
Al-Maturidi demonstrates that claiming humans can thwart God's will is blasphemous because it implies God can be made foolish and powerless.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, are you aware that you are effectively challenging God's decree? How does this passage's warning about making God foolish change how you view your next act of disobedience?
?
Even the most foolish human would not make a decree as absurd as the one described. Why do we sometimes think God's commands are unreasonable? What does that reveal about your trust in His wisdom?
?
The passage says that believing in independent human power gives humans superiority over God. Do you ever feel proud of your choices as if they are solely yours? How can you actively attribute your success to God's grace without diminishing your responsibility?

Power Prior to Action Would Make Humans Independent of God
Al-Maturidi argues against pre-existing powers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Al-Maturidi's argument against pre-existing powers and its implications for human dependence on God.

Core Idea
Pre-existing powers would make humans independent of God, contradicting our inherent neediness.

Al-Maturidi presents a sharp theological argument: if humans possessed power before acting, they would not need God to create those actions. But the Quran teaches that all creation is needy before God. This passage uses rational and scriptural reasoning to defend divine transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the literal translation. Let the argument's flow sink in.
Notice the compact style of Al-Maturidi.
2
Identify the two premises
The argument has two key premises: (1) if powers existed before action, humans would be independent; (2) God made all creation needy. Find these in the text.
Premise 1 is conditional, premise 2 is a statement about God's nature.
3
Understand the conclusion
The conclusion is that such independence is impermissible and 'ugly in hearing'. Reflect on why this is a strong conclusion.
This conclusion is both rational and scriptural.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضا أن القوى لو كانت لأحوال تردا لكان بها يستغنى عن الله في جميع الأفعال قبل وجود الأفعال ، والله جل ثناؤه صير الخلق جميعا فقراء إليه وهو الغنى الحميد ، لم يجز أن يقع لهم الغنى عنه بأحق ما لزمتنا الحاجة ، والأصل أنها إذ كانت لا تبقى تزول حاجة البقاء والفعل ليس بموجود فيصير غنيا عن قبل كونه ، وذلك قبيح فى السمع ، ولا قوة إلا بالله
And also that if powers were for states that come, they would by them be independent of God in all actions before the existence of actions, and God, exalted be His praise, made all creation needy to Him and He is the independent, the praised; it is not permissible that they become independent of Him by the most rightful that necessitates need for us. And the principle: since they do not endure, the need for endurance ceases and the action does not exist, so he becomes independent before its existence, and that is ugly in hearing, and there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 860

Commentary
This passage is an argument against the view that powers (quwa/قوى) exist as states prior to actions. The author asserts that if such powers existed before actions, humans would be independent of God for those actions, contradicting the fact that God made all creation needy (fuqara/فقراء) to Him. He notes that since powers (as accidents) do not endure, the need for endurance ceases, and since the action is not yet existent, the agent would be independent before the action, which is rationally repugnant (qabih fi al-sam'/قبيح في السمع).

Key Terms
قوى
فقراء
غنى
حاجة
قبيح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Pre-existing powers are necessary for action.
Correction: Al-Maturidi argues that pre-existing powers would lead to human independence from God, contradicting our inherent neediness.

Checkpoint
What would be the consequence of powers existing before actions, according to Al-Maturidi?
A) Humans would be more obedient
B) Humans would become independent of God
C) Actions would be impossible
D) God's power would increase

Key Takeaway
Pre-existing powers would make humans independent of God, contradicting our neediness and divine transcendence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you perform a simple action like raising your hand, do you feel a sense of need for God's power in that moment, or do you assume the power is already yours? How would your awareness of God change if you truly believed every action depended on His immediate creation of power?
?
Al-Maturidi says it is 'ugly in hearing' for a human to become independent of God even before an action exists. In what areas of your life do you act as if you already possess the power to succeed, without consciously relying on God? What would it mean to repent of that independence and actively depend on Him for your next action?
?
If you truly internalized that you are 'needy' (faqr) to God for every breath and movement, how would that change your morning routine, your work, your interactions with others? Name one specific habit you will change today to live out this constant need for God.

The First View: Capacity Suitable for Both Obedience and Disobedience
Maturidi presents the first view on capacity for opposites and its justification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first position on capacity for opposites, as held by Abu Hanifa and the Mu'tazila, and its implication for the doctrine of taklif ma la yutaq.

Core Idea
Capacity for an act can serve both obedience and its opposite, otherwise commands would be impossible.

Maturidi begins this chapter by presenting a key disagreement: is the power that enables obedience also fit for disobedience? The first group, including Abu Hanifa, says yes. This lesson unpacks their reasoning and the theological stakes of this claim.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening passage
Read the first part where Maturidi introduces the disagreement and the first group's view.
Focus on the claim that capacity is suitable for both.
2
Understand the implication for Mu'tazila
Notice that Maturidi says this view is confirmed by the Mu'tazila and leads to 'actualizing what is not possible' (tahqīq mā lā yuṭāq).
This is a key polemical point.
3
Examine the reasoning
Trace the argument: if capacity were not suitable for both, then when a person is commanded and prohibited at the same time, they would lack capacity.
The necessity of capacity for opposites is argued from the coexistence of command and prohibition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة
القول في صلاحية القدرة للضدين وتكليف ما لا يطاق
قال الفقيه أبو منصور رحمه الله: ثم اختلف أهل هذا القول في قوة الطاعة أهى تصلح للمعصية أم لا. قال جماعة: هي تصلح للأمرين جميعا، وهو قول أبي حنيفة وجماعته. وهذا القول أثبته جميع [أهل] الاعتزال عند التأمل، ويحقق عليهم القول بتحقيق ما لا يطاق، وذلك سببهم في القول بتقدم القوة، والله الموفق. وأصل هذا أنه لما كان سبب من أسباب القول يصلح للشيء وضده فكذلك القدرة، مع ما في نفي [أن يصلح للأمرين] فوت القدرة على فعل ضد الذي جاء به، وقد يؤمر به وينهى عنه في وقته، فيلزم القول بالقدرة على الشيء وضده، ليكون الأمر والنهي على الوسع والقوة، ولا قوة إلا بالله.
ثم الأصل أن كل شيء يصلح لشيء لا يصلح لضده، فيكون الذي به بالطبع لا بالاختيار، ولو كانت القوة لا تصلح لهما لكان ما كان يقع بالطبع لا بالاختيار، ولا قوة إلا بالله.
وقال جماعة منهم: قوة الطاعة هي غير قوة المعصية، منهم الحسين وغيره يذهبون إلى أن قوة الطاعة التوفيق والعصمة، وقوة المعصية الخذلان والترك على ما يختار؛ ودليل ذلك وجود سؤال المعونة والعصمة، على الإحاطة أن ليس معهما زيغ، والتوفيق على الإحاطة أن معه الإصابة، وكذلك القول الظاهر باللهم قوني على طاعتك وأعني عليها، وبتعوذ من الخذلان والإزاغة، ثبت لو كان يكون بكل واحد منها ما يكون بالآخر لم يكن الذي يسأل بالسؤال أحق من الذي
Question: The statement on the suitability of capacity (qudra) for opposites and the obligation of what is not possible (taklīf mā lā yuṭāq).
Al-Faqīh Abū Manṣūr (may Allah have mercy on him) said: Then the people of this statement differed concerning the power (quwwa) of obedience: is it suitable for disobedience or not? A group said: It is suitable for both matters, and that is the statement of Abū Ḥanīfa and his group. And this statement is confirmed by all [the people] of Mu'tazila upon reflection, and it necessitates for them the statement of actualizing what is not possible, and that is their reason for the statement of the precedence of power (taqaddum al-quwwa). And Allah is the Giver of success. And the origin of this is that since a cause from among the causes of the statement is suitable for a thing and its opposite, so too is capacity. Moreover, in negating [that it is suitable for both] is the loss of capacity to do the opposite of what one has brought, and he may be commanded with it and prohibited from it in its time, so the statement of capacity for a thing and its opposite becomes necessary, so that the command and prohibition are within capacity and power. And there is no power except by Allah.
Then the principle is that every thing that is suitable for a thing is not suitable for its opposite, so that which is by it would be by nature (bi-l-ṭabʿ) not by choice (bi-l-ikhtiyār). And if the power (quwwa) were not suitable for both, then whatever occurs would occur by nature not by choice. And there is no power except by Allah.
And a group among them said: The power of obedience is other than the power of disobedience. Among them is al-Ḥusayn and others who go to the view that the power of obedience is tawfīq (divine facilitation) and ʿiṣma (protection), and the power of disobedience is khidhlān (abandonment) and tark (leaving) upon what one chooses. And the evidence for that is the existence of the request for aid (maʿūna) and protection (ʿiṣma), with the encompassing (al-iḥāṭa) that there is no deviation (zaygh) with them, and tawfīq with the encompassing that with it is correctness (iṣāba). Likewise the apparent statement: 'O Allah, strengthen me for Your obedience and help me upon it,' and seeking refuge from khidhlān and izāgha (misguidance). It is established that if each one of them had the same effect as the other, then the one who asks would not be more entitled by the request than the one who
Source pages p. 862

Commentary
This passage is a classification and discussion of two views on the suitability of capacity for opposites and its relation to taklīf mā lā yuṭāq (obligation of what is not possible). Maturidi begins by stating that the people of this statement (i.e., those who accept capacity) differed on whether the power (quwwa) for obedience is also suitable for disobedience. The first group, including Abu Hanifa, holds that it is suitable for both. Maturidi notes that this view is actually confirmed by all Mu'tazila upon reflection, and it leads to the doctrine of 'actualizing what is not possible' (tahqīq mā lā yuṭāq), which is the basis for their claim of the precedence of power (taqaddum al-quwwa). He explains the reasoning: since a cause is suitable for a thing and its opposite, so is capacity. Denying this would mean loss of capacity to do the opposite of what one has done, yet the person may be commanded and prohibited at the same time, so capacity for both is necessary for command and prohibition to be within capacity and power. Maturidi then presents the contrary principle: if something is suitable for one thing, it is not suitable for its opposite; otherwise, it would be by nature (bi-l-ṭabʿ) not by choice (bi-l-ikhtiyār). He concludes that if power were not suitable for both, actions would be determined by nature. Next, he presents the second group's view: the power of obedience is distinct from the power of disobedience. They identify the power of obedience as tawfīq (divine facilitation) and ʿiṣma (protection), and the power of disobedience as khidhlān (divine abandonment) and tark (leaving one to his choice). The evidence includes supplications: asking for aid (maʿūna) and protection, and seeking refuge from khidhlān and izāgha (misguidance). The argument is that such prayers would be meaningless if one capacity served both purposes; the one who asks would not be more entitled than the one who does not.

Key Terms
قدرة (qudra)
قوة (quwwa)
طاعة (ṭāʿa)
معصية (maʿṣiya)
ضد (ḍidd)
تكليف ما لا يطاق (taklīf mā lā yuṭāq)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Capacity for an act is only sufficient for that act and not its opposite, so commands to avoid something while doing it are impossible.
Correction: Maturidi argues that if capacity were not suitable for both, then when commanded and prohibited simultaneously, one would lack capacity, but this is avoided by seeing capacity as suitable for both.

Checkpoint
According to the first group (Abu Hanifa), what is the power (quwwa) of obedience suitable for?
Only obedience
Only disobedience
Both obedience and disobedience
Neither

Key Takeaway
The first view, held by Abu Hanifa and the Mu'tazila, asserts that the same capacity is suitable for both obedience and disobedience, which is necessary for command and prohibition to be within one's capability.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have learned that your capacity is equally suitable for obedience and disobedience. When you choose to sin, do you ever blame your circumstances or lack of ability? How does this teaching hold you accountable for your choices?
?
If you truly believe that at the moment of a command you have the capacity to obey, what stops you from obeying immediately? Will you now, in the next moment of temptation, act on that capacity?
?
The passage ends with 'there is no power except by Allah.' Does this humble you to seek His help while acknowledging your own responsibility? How will you rely on Him more in your next act of obedience?

The Second View: Distinct Powers for Obedience and Disobedience
Maturidi presents the second view distinguishing powers and the supplication evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second position on capacity for opposites, which distinguishes the power of obedience from the power of disobedience, and its evidential basis in supplications.

Core Idea
Obedience and disobedience rely on different divine gifts: tawfiq and isma vs. khidhlan and tark.

After presenting the first view, Maturidi turns to a second group led by al-Husayn. They argue that the power for obedience is qualitatively different from the power for disobedience. Their evidence comes from the very prayers believers make, asking for help in obedience and seeking refuge from misguidance. This lesson explores that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the second group's statement
Read the part where Maturidi says 'وقال جماعة منهم: قوة الطاعة هي غير قوة المعصية'.
Note the identification of each power with distinct concepts: tawfiq/isma vs. khidhlan/tark.
2
Understand the identification
The group defines the power of obedience as divine facilitation (tawfiq) and protection (isma), and the power of disobedience as divine abandonment (khidhlan) and leaving to choice (tark).
This frames the capacities as divine interventions, not inherent human powers.
3
Analyze the supplication evidence
The group cites prayers like 'O Allah, strengthen me for Your obedience' and seeking refuge from khidhlan and izagha. The argument: if one power served both, these prayers would be unnecessary or misdirected.
The prayer differentiates between the source of obedience and disobedience.

Source Text

?

?
If your prayers for ʿiṣma are sincere, why do you sometimes still feel safe in your obedience? What would it look like to beg Allah daily for protection as if your next sin depends entirely on His gift?

Divine Decree
intermediate

One Power for Both Obedience and Disobedience
Maturidi presents the first view that one power is suitable for both obedience and disobedience.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the reasoning behind the view that a single power is suitable for both obedience and disobedience, and how this view relates to the concepts of natural inclination and choice.

Core Idea
If power were not for both, actions would be by nature, not by choice.

Imam Maturidi begins his discussion on human capability by presenting the view held by Abu Hanifa and his followers: that one and the same power is sufficient for both acts of obedience and acts of disobedience. This is not just a theological opinion; it has profound implications for understanding moral responsibility, divine commands, and the nature of human choice. In this passage, Maturidi lays out the reasoning behind this position and warns of the consequences if it were rejected.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the main claim
Read the Arabic text and its translation carefully. Note that Maturidi attributes this view to Abu Hanifa and his group, and mentions that the Mu'tazila also affirm it.
2
Trace the argument from cause to power
Maturidi draws an analogy: if a cause is suitable for a thing and its opposite, then power (qudra) must be likewise. Follow his reasoning step by step, especially the part about command and prohibition at the same time.
The text has a slightly unclear phrase 'مع ما في نفى ما في نفى' which may be a scribal duplication; focus on the overall argument.
3
Reflect on the principle of suitability and choice
Maturidi then states a general principle: anything suitable for one thing is not suitable for its opposite would be by nature, not choice. Consider how this supports the first position and what it implies about human agency.
The passage ends with 'ولا قوة إلا بالله' emphasizing divine source of power.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الفقيه أبو منصور رحمه الله :: ثم اختلف أهل هذا القول في قوة الطاعه أهى تصلح للمعصية أم لا . قال جماعة : هى تصلح للامرين جميعا ، وهو قول أبى حنيفة وجماعته . وهذا القول أثبته جميع أهل الاعتزال عند التأمل ، ويحقق عليهم القول بتحقيق ما لا يطاق، وذلك سببهم فى القول بتقدم القوة ، والله الموفق . وأصل هذا أنه لما كان سبب من أسباب القول يصلح للشيء وضده فكذلك القدرة ، مع ما في نفى ما في نفى أن يصلح للأمرين فوت القدرة على فعل ضد الذي جاء به ، وقد يؤمر به وينهى عنه في وقته ، فيلزم القول بالقدرة على الشيء وضده ، ليكون الأمر والنهى على الوسع والقوة ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . ثم الأصل أن كل شيء يصلح لشيء لا يصلح لضده ، فيكون الذي به بالطبع لا بالاختيار ، ولو كانت القوة لا تصلح لهما لكان ما كان يقع بالطبع لا بالاختيار ، ولا قوة إلا بالله .
The jurist Abu Mansur, may Allah have mercy on him, said: Then the people of this saying differed concerning the power for obedience—whether it is suitable for disobedience or not. A group said: It is suitable for both matters entirely, and this is the saying of Abu Hanifa and his group. And all the Mu'tazila, upon examination, affirmed this saying, and it realizes upon them the saying of imposing what cannot be borne, and that is their reason for saying the priority of power, and Allah is the granter of success. The origin of this is that when something is a cause of the causes of a saying and is suitable for a thing and its opposite, then power is likewise, along with what is in the negation of that it is suitable for both—loss of power over the act of the opposite of that which one came with. And one may be commanded and forbidden regarding it at its time, so it necessitates saying that power is for the thing and its opposite, so that the command and prohibition are within capacity and strength, and there is no power except by Allah. Then the origin is that everything that is suitable for one thing is not suitable for its opposite, then that which is by it would be by nature, not by choice. And if power were not suitable for both, then that which occurs would occur by nature, not by choice, and there is no power except by Allah.
Source pages p. 862

Commentary
This passage presents the first position in a debate about whether the power (quwwa) for obedience is the same as that for disobedience. Maturidi begins by stating that a group, including Abu Hanifa and his followers, holds that one and the same power is suitable for both obedience and disobedience. He notes that the Mu'tazila also affirm this upon examination, which leads them to the doctrine of imposing what cannot be borne (taklif ma la yutaq) and the priority of power (taqaddum al-quwwa). The reasoning is that if a cause is suitable for both a thing and its opposite, then the power (qudra) must be likewise. If one denies that the power is suitable for both, then one loses the power to perform the opposite act of what one has come to do. Furthermore, since a person can be commanded and forbidden at the same time regarding the same act, it necessitates that power be for both the thing and its opposite, so that command and prohibition are within one's capacity. The author then establishes a general principle: anything that is suitable for one thing is not suitable for its opposite—that would be by nature (tab'), not choice (ikhtiyar). If power were not suitable for both, then actions would be by nature rather than by choice. The passage ends with the reminder that all power is from Allah.

Key Terms
طاعة (obedience)
معصية (disobedience)
قوة (power)
قدرة (capability)
تكليف ما لا يطاق (imposition of what cannot be borne)
طبع (nature)
اختيار (choice)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the view that one power is suitable for both opposites implies human power is independent of Allah.
Correction: The text repeatedly affirms 'لا قوة إلا بالله' (there is no power except by Allah), indicating that all power is divinely sourced.

Checkpoint
According to the first position presented, what is the consequence if power were not suitable for both obedience and disobedience?
A) It would lead to the impossibility of command and prohibition.
B) Actions would occur by nature, not by choice.
C) Power would have to exist for two moments.
D) The Mu'tazila would reject the priority of power.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi establishes that if power were not suitable for both obedience and disobedience, human actions would be by nature rather than by choice, undermining moral responsibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you honestly acknowledge that you had the same power that could have been used for obedience? What does that say about your choices?
?
Is there an area of your life where you blame your 'nature' or circumstances for your actions? How does this lesson demand you take full responsibility for your choices?
?
If all power is from Allah, how does that change the way you approach both your obedience and your failures? Will you turn to Him for power to obey?
